## MANDATORY: Use Sourcegraph MCP Tools

You have Sourcegraph MCP tools available for this task. Using these tools is a **required part of solving this task** — not optional.

### REQUIRED: Use Deep Search (`mcp__sourcegraph__sg_deepsearch`)

You have access to **Deep Search** — a powerful semantic code analysis tool. You **MUST** use it as your **first action** when starting this task, before any other exploration.

**Step 0 (BEFORE everything else):** Run `mcp__sourcegraph__sg_deepsearch` with a query describing what this task requires. For example:
- "How does [feature/component from the task] work in this codebase?"
- "Where is [concept from the task] implemented and what are its dependencies?"
- "Trace the code path for [operation described in the task]"

Deep Search understands code semantically — it traces call chains, data flows, and architectural relationships across files. It is **far more effective** than keyword search for understanding how code fits together.

**When to use Deep Search (mandatory for all of these):**
- Understanding how a feature or subsystem works end-to-end
- Tracing data flow or request lifecycle across multiple files
- Finding all the places that need to change for a cross-cutting modification
- Understanding architectural relationships before making changes
- Any time you need to understand "how does X work?" or "what calls Y?"

**Use `mcp__sourcegraph__sg_deepsearch_read`** to retrieve the full content of any Deep Search result.

Do NOT skip Deep Search and jump straight to keyword search or file browsing. Deep Search gives you the architectural context you need to solve the task correctly.


### Step 1 (REQUIRED before any code changes):
Before you read, edit, or write ANY code, you MUST first use Sourcegraph MCP to explore the codebase:
1. Use `mcp__sourcegraph__sg_list_files` to understand the project structure
2. Use `mcp__sourcegraph__sg_keyword_search` to locate the relevant code for this task
3. Use `mcp__sourcegraph__sg_read_file` to read key files through Sourcegraph

### Step 2: Continue using MCP throughout
- Instead of Grep -> use `mcp__sourcegraph__sg_keyword_search`
- Instead of Glob -> use `mcp__sourcegraph__sg_list_files`

If you catch yourself reaching for Grep or Glob to *find* code, STOP and use Sourcegraph instead.
The only acceptable use of Grep/Glob is verifying content in a file you already located via Sourcegraph.

     8→
     9→
    10→class Print(HigherOrderOperator):
    11→    """
    12→    print(format_str, **kwargs) -> None
    13→
    14→    This Higher Order Operator (HOP) provides a functional version of print for use in PyTorch graphs.
    15→    It enables format printing with named arguments, e.g., torch._higher_order_ops.print("moo {x} {y}", x=1, y=2).
    16→
    17→    This HOP enables printing without causing graph break.
    18→    """
    19→
    20→    def __init__(self) -> None:
    21→        super().__init__("print")
    22→
    23→    def __call__(self, format_str: str, **kwargs: object) -> None:
    24→        assert isinstance(format_str, str)
    25→        return super().__call__(format_str, **kwargs)
    26→
    27→    # pyrefly: ignore [bad-override]
    28→    def gen_schema(self, format_str: str, **kwargs: object) -> torch.FunctionSchema:
    29→        from torch._higher_order_ops.schema import HopSchemaGenerator
    30→
    31→        schema_gen = HopSchemaGenerator(self)
    32→        schema_gen.add_arg("format_str", format_str[0])
    33→
    34→        # Add each kwarg as a keyword-only argument
    35→        for key, value in kwargs.items():
    36→            schema_gen.add_arg(key, value, kw_only=True)
    37→
    38→        schema_gen.add_schema_tree_spec(format_str, **kwargs)
    39→
    40→        return schema_gen.gen_schema()
    41→
    42→
    43→print = Print()
    44→
    45→
    46→@print.py_impl(ProxyTorchDispatchMode)

    32→def _get_op_qualname(op: _op_identifier) -> str:
    33→    """Convert an op identifier to a qualified string key."""
    34→    if isinstance(op, torch._ops.OpOverload):
    35→        return op._name
    36→    elif isinstance(op, torch._ops.HigherOrderOperator):
    37→        return f"{op.namespace}::{op.name()}"
    38→    elif isinstance(op, CustomOpDef):
    39→        return op._qualname
    40→    elif isinstance(op, str):
    41→        return op
    42→
    43→    raise ValueError(f"Invalid operator input {op}")

## Summary

I have implemented the fix for issue #167368 - "[HOP][print]Add functionalize and side effect". The changes add support for `*args` (positional arguments) to the print Higher Order Primitive and add the functionalization implementation for `with_effects`.

### Files Modified:

1. **`torch/_higher_order_ops/print.py`** (59 additions, 22 deletions):
   - Updated `Print` class docstring to document support for positional args
   - Updated `__call__` to accept `*args` in addition to `**kwargs`
   - Updated `gen_schema` to handle positional args with naming convention `arg0`, `arg1`, etc.
   - Updated `print_proxy_torch_dispatch_mode` to handle `*args`
   - Updated `print_fake_tensor_mode` to handle `*args`
   - Updated `print_impl` (CompositeExplicitAutograd) to format with both `*args` and `**kwargs`
   - Updated `print_func` (functionalize impl) to pass `*args` through `handle_effects`

2. **`torch/_higher_order_ops/effects.py`** (55 additions, 23 deletions):
   - Added `@with_effects.py_functionalize_impl` decorator with `with_effects_functional` function that re-emits with_effects since it's already functional
   - Replaced `assert` statements with explicit `raise AssertionError` for better error messages
   - Updated error handling in `handle_effects` with descriptive error messages

3. **`test/higher_order_ops/test_print.py`** (significant expansion):
   - Added comprehensive tests for positional args, kwargs, and mixed args/kwargs
   - Updated existing tests to include positional args format
   - Added tests for Inductor fusion patterns w

What files implement the print operator and how does functionalization handle side effects?\\nshare_url: https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/deepsearch/ca6c53ba-d360-400d-a650-b54961d37bfb\\ncreated: 2026-02-05T22:25:51Z\\nupdated: 2026-02-05T22:26:34Z\\n---\\n\\n# How does the print HOP (Higher Order Primitive) work in PyTorch, specifically regarding functionalize and side effects? What files implement the print operator and how does functionalization handle side effects?\\n\\nPerfect! Now I have a complete understanding. Let me provide you with a comprehensive answer.\\n\\n## How the Print HOP Works in PyTorch\\n\\nThe print Higher Order Primitive (HOP) in PyTorch enables side-effectful printing within traced graphs (e.g., AOTAutograd, TorchDynamo) without causing graph breaks. Here's how it handles functionalization and side effects:\\n\\n### Key Implementation Files\\n\\n1. **[torch/_higher_order_ops/print.py](https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/pytorch/pytorch/-/blob/torch/_higher_order_ops/print.py)** - Core print HOP definition\\n2. **[torch/_higher_order_ops/effects.py](https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/pytorch/pytorch/-/blob/torch/_higher_order_ops/effects.py)** - Side effect handling system\\n3. **[torch/_higher_order_ops/base_hop.py](https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/pytorch/pytorch/-/blob/torch/_higher_order_ops/base_hop.py)** - Base HOP infrastructure\\n\\n### How Functionalization Handles Side Effects\\n\\nThe system uses **effect tokens** to maintain execution order during functionalization:\\n\\n#### 1. **Print Registration as an Effectful Op**\\n\\nIn [effects.py:64](https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/pytorch/pytorch/-/blob/torch/_higher_order_ops/effects.py?L64):\\n\\n```python\\n_register_effectful_op(hop_print, _EffectType.ORDERED)\\n```\\n\\nThis registers `print` as having ordered side effects, meaning multiple print calls must execute in order.\\n\\n#### 2. **Functionalization Implementation**\\n\\nWhen the print HOP is encountered during functionalization, the `print_func` handler is called ([print.py:106-116](https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/pytorch/pytorch/-/blob/torch/_higher_order_ops/print.py?L106-116)):\\n\\n```python\\n@print.py_functionalize_impl\\ndef print_func(ctx, format_str: str, *args: object, **kwargs: object):\\n    from torch._higher_order_ops.effects import handle_effects\\n\\n    return handle_effects(\\n        ctx.mode._allow_token_discovery,\\n        ctx.mode._tokens,\\n        print,\\n        (format_str, *args),\\n        kwargs,\\n    )\\n```\\n\\n#### 3. **The Effect Token System**\\n\\nThe `handle_effects` function ([effects.py:230-325](https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/pytorch/pytorch/-/blob/torch/_higher_order_ops/effects.py?L230-325)) implements the token threading mechanism:\\n\\n```python\\ndef handle_effects(\\n    allow_token_discovery: bool,\\n    tokens: dict[_EffectType, torch.Tensor],\\n    op: OpType,\\n    args: tuple[Any, ...],\\n    kwargs: dict[str, Any],\\n) -> Any:\\n```\\n\\n**Key steps:**\\n\\n1. **Get or create a token** - Tokens are dummy tensors (`torch.tensor([])`) that represent effect types\\n2. **Wrap the op with `with_effects`** - The print call gets wrapped in a `with_effects` HOP:\\n   ```python\\n   (new_token, *unwrapped_outs) = with_effects(\\n       unwrapped_token, op, *unwrapped_args, **unwrapped_kwargs\\n   )\\n   ```\\n3. **Thread the token** - The new token is stored back in the tokens map, creating a data dependency chain\\n\\n#### 4. **The `with_effects` HOP**\\n\\nDefined in [effects.py:67-103](https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/pytorch/pytorch/-/blob/torch/_higher_order_ops/effects.py?L67-103):\\n\\n```python\\nclass WithEffects(HigherOrderOperator):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    with_effects(token, op, args, kwargs) -> (new_token, op_results)\\n    \\n    This HOP helps ensure ordering between side effectful ops like prints or ops\\n    using torchbind objects. This is done through threading \\\"effect tokens\\\" through the\\n    graph to enforce data dependence between side effectful ops.\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n```\\n\\nThe actual implementation ([effects.py:132-149](https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/pytorch/pytorch/-/blob/torch/_higher_order_ops/effects.py?L132-149)) executes the op and creates a new token:\\n\\n```python\\n@with_effects.py_impl(DispatchKey.CompositeExplicitAutograd)\\ndef with_effects_dense(\\n    token: torch.Tensor,\\n    op: torch._ops.OpOverload,\\n    *args: tuple[Any, ...],\\n    **kwargs: dict[str, Any],\\n) -> tuple[torch.Tensor, ...]:\\n    out = op(*args, **kwargs)\\n    new_token = new_token_tensor()\\n    if isinstance(out, tuple):\\n        return (new_token, *out)\\n    return (new_token, out)\\n```\\n\\n### Visual Example\\n\\nHere's what happens when you use print in a compiled function:\\n\\n**Original code:**\\n```python\\ndef f(x):\\n    torch._higher_order_ops.print(\\\"moo {x}\\\", x=1)\\n    res = x + x\\n    torch._higher_order_ops.print(\\\"result {}\\\", res)\\n    return res\\n```\\n\\n**After functionalization (AOT Autograd):**\\n```python\\ndef forward(self, token, x):\\n    # First print wrapped with token\\n    with_effects = torch.ops.higher_order.with_effects(\\n        token, torch.ops.higher_order.print, 'moo {x}', x=1\\n    )\\n    token1 = with_effects[0]\\n    \\n    # Computation\\n    res = x + x\\n    \\n    # Second print depends on first via token1\\n    with_effects_1 = torch.ops.higher_order.with_effects(\\n        token1, torch.ops.higher_order.print, 'result {}', res\\n    )\\n    token2 = with_effects_1[0]\\n    \\n    return (token2, res)\\n```\\n\\n### Why This Matters\\n\\n1. **Prevents reordering** - The token dependencies ensure prints execute in the correct order even through aggressive optimizations\\n2. **Prevents DCE (Dead Code Elimination)** - The token threading prevents prints from being eliminated as \\\"unused\\\" operations\\n3. **Maintains functional graph semantics** - The graph appears functional (no true side effects) while preserving the intended side-effectful behavior\\n\\n### Token Creation and Discovery\\n\\nFrom [effects.py:256-284](https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/pytorch/pytorch/-/blob/torch/_higher_order_ops/effects.py?L256-284):\\n\\n- **During forward pass**: Tokens are created eagerly if `allow_token_discovery=True`\\n- **During backward pass**: New tokens can be discovered and added as graph placeholders\\n- **In Inductor**: Tokens are created with `_make_token` and cleaned up with `_sink_tokens`\\n\\nThis elegant design allows PyTorch to support side effects in compiled graphs while maintaining the benefits of functional programming for optimization passes.\\n\\n## Sources\\n\\n- [github.com/pytorch/pytorch/torch/_higher_order_ops/print.py@f28ea69](/github.com/pytorch/pytorch@f28ea6906201a754b307bc1d31b96d2ec05a912a/-/blob/torch/_higher_order_ops/print.py)\\n- [github.com/pytorch/pytorch/torch/_higher_order_ops/effects.py@f28ea69](/github.com/pytorch/pytorch@f28ea6906201a754b307bc1d31b96d2ec05a912a/-/blob/torch/_higher_order_ops/effects.py)\\n- [github.com/pytorch/pytorch/torch/_higher_order_ops/base_hop.py@f28ea69](/github.com/pytorch/pytorch@f28ea6906201a754b307bc1d31b96d2ec05a912a/-/blob/torch/_higher_order_ops/base_hop.py)\\n- [repo:^github.com/pytorch/pytorch$ _higher_order_ops.print](/search?q=patterntype:keyword%20repo:%5Egithub.com%2Fpytorch%2Fpytorch$%20_higher_order_ops.print)\\n- [github.com/pytorch/pytorch/test/higher_order_ops/test_print.py@f28ea69](/github.com/pytorch/pytorch@f28ea6906201a754b307bc1d31b96d2ec05a912a/-/blob/test/higher_order_ops/test_print.py)\\n\\n\"}",

Let me provide you with a comprehensive answer.\n\n## How the Print HOP Works in PyTorch\n\nThe print Higher Order Primitive (HOP) in PyTorch enables side-effectful printing within traced graphs (e.g., AOTAutograd, TorchDynamo) without causing graph breaks. Here's how it handles functionalization and side effects:\n\n### Key Implementation Files\n\n1. **[torch/_higher_order_ops/print.py](https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/pytorch/pytorch/-/blob/torch/_higher_order_ops/print.py)** - Core print HOP definition\n2. **[torch/_higher_order_ops/effects.py](https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/pytorch/pytorch/-/blob/torch/_higher_order_ops/effects.py)** - Side effect handling system\n3. **[torch/_higher_order_ops/base_hop.py](https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/pytorch/pytorch/-/blob/torch/_higher_order_ops/base_hop.py)** - Base HOP infrastructure\n\n### How Functionalization Handles Side Effects\n\nThe system uses **effect tokens** to maintain execution order during functionalization:\n\n#### 1. **Print Registration as an Effectful Op**\n\nIn [effects.py:64](https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/pytorch/pytorch/-/blob/torch/_higher_order_ops/effects.py?L64):\n\n```python\n_register_effectful_op(hop_print, _EffectType.ORDERED)\n```\n\nThis registers `print` as having ordered side effects, meaning multiple print calls must execute in order.\n\n#### 2. **Functionalization Implementation**\n\nWhen the print HOP is encountered during functionalization, the `print_func` handler is called ([print.py:106-116](https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/pytorch/pytorch/-/blob/torch/_higher_order_ops/print.py?L106-116)):\n\n```python\n@print.py_functionalize_impl\ndef print_func(ctx, format_str: str, *args: object, **kwargs: object):\n    from torch._higher_order_ops.effects import handle_effects\n\n    return handle_effects(\n        ctx.mode._allow_token_discovery,\n        ctx.mode._tokens,\n        print,\n        (format_str, *args),\n        kwargs,\n    )\n```\n\n#### 3. **The Effect Token System**\n\nThe `handle_effects` function ([effects.py:230-325](https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/pytorch/pytorch/-/blob/torch/_higher_order_ops/effects.py?L230-325)) implements the token threading mechanism:\n\n```python\ndef handle_effects(\n    allow_token_discovery: bool,\n    tokens: dict[_EffectType, torch.Tensor],\n    op: OpType,\n    args: tuple[Any, ...],\n    kwargs: dict[str, Any],\n) -> Any:\n```\n\n**Key steps:**\n\n1. **Get or create a token** - Tokens are dummy tensors (`torch.tensor([])`) that represent effect types\n2. **Wrap the op with `with_effects`** - The print call gets wrapped in a `with_effects` HOP:\n   ```python\n   (new_token, *unwrapped_outs) = with_effects(\n       unwrapped_token, op, *unwrapped_args, **unwrapped_kwargs\n   )\n   ```\n3. **Thread the token** - The new token is stored back in the tokens map, creating a data dependency chain\n\n#### 4. **The `with_effects` HOP**\n\nDefined in [effects.py:67-103](https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/pytorch/pytorch/-/blob/torch/_higher_order_ops/effects.py?L67-103):\n\n```python\nclass WithEffects(HigherOrderOperator):\n    \"\"\"\n    with_effects(token, op, args, kwargs) -> (new_token, op_results)\n    \n    This HOP helps ensure ordering between side effectful ops like prints or ops\n    using torchbind objects. This is done through threading \"effect tokens\" through the\n    graph to enforce data dependence between side effectful ops.\n    \"\"\"\n```\n\nThe actual implementation ([effects.py:132-149](https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/pytorch/pytorch/-/blob/torch/_higher_order_ops/effects.py?L132-149)) executes the op and creates a new token:\n\n```python\n@with_effects.py_impl(DispatchKey.CompositeExplicitAutograd)\ndef with_effects_dense(\n    token: torch.Tensor,\n    op: torch._ops.OpOverload,\n    *args: tuple[Any, ...],\n    **kwargs: dict[str, Any],\n) -> tuple[torch.Tensor, ...]:\n    out = op(*args, **kwargs)\n    new_token = new_token_tensor()\n    if isinstance(out, tuple):\n        return (new_token, *out)\n    return (new_token, out)\n```\n\n### Visual Example\n\nHere's what happens when you use print in a compiled function:\n\n**Original code:**\n```python\ndef f(x):\n    torch._higher_order_ops.print(\"moo {x}\", x=1)\n    res = x + x\n    torch._higher_order_ops.print(\"result {}\", res)\n    return res\n```\n\n**After functionalization (AOT Autograd):**\n```python\ndef forward(self, token, x):\n    # First print wrapped with token\n    with_effects = torch.ops.higher_order.with_effects(\n        token, torch.ops.higher_order.print, 'moo {x}', x=1\n    )\n    token1 = with_effects[0]\n    \n    # Computation\n    res = x + x\n    \n    # Second print depends on first via token1\n    with_effects_1 = torch.ops.higher_order.with_effects(\n        token1, torch.ops.higher_order.print, 'result {}', res\n    )\n    token2 = with_effects_1[0]\n    \n    return (token2, res)\n```\n\n### Why This Matters\n\n1. **Prevents reordering** - The token dependencies ensure prints execute in the correct order even through aggressive optimizations\n2. **Prevents DCE (Dead Code Elimination)** - The token threading prevents prints from being eliminated as \"unused\" operations\n3. **Maintains functional graph semantics** - The graph appears functional (no true side effects) while preserving the intended side-effectful behavior\n\n### Token Creation and Discovery\n\nFrom [effects.py:256-284](https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/pytorch/pytorch/-/blob/torch/_higher_order_ops/effects.py?L256-284):\n\n- **During forward pass**: Tokens are created eagerly if `allow_token_discovery=True`\n- **During backward pass**: New tokens can be discovered and added as graph placeholders\n- **In Inductor**: Tokens are created with `_make_token` and cleaned up with `_sink_tokens`\n\nThis elegant design allows PyTorch to support side effects in compiled graphs while maintaining the benefits of functional programming for optimization passes.\n\n## Sources\n\n- [github.com/pytorch/pytorch/torch/_higher_order_ops/print.py@f28ea69](/github.com/pytorch/pytorch@f28ea6906201a754b307bc1d31b96d2ec05a912a/-/blob/torch/_higher_order_ops/print.py)\n- [github.com/pytorch/pytorch/torch/_higher_order_ops/effects.py@f28ea69](/github.com/pytorch/pytorch@f28ea6906201a754b307bc1d31b96d2ec05a912a/-/blob/torch/_higher_order_ops/effects.py)\n- [github.com/pytorch/pytorch/torch/_higher_order_ops/base_hop.py@f28ea69](/github.com/pytorch/pytorch@f28ea6906201a754b307bc1d31b96d2ec05a912a/-/blob/torch/_higher_order_ops/base_hop.py)\n- [repo:^github.com/pytorch/pytorch$ _higher_order_ops.print](/search?q=patterntype:keyword%20repo:%5Egithub.com%2Fpytorch%2Fpytorch$%20_higher_order_ops.print)\n- [github.com/pytorch/pytorch/test/higher_order_ops/test_print.py@f28ea69](/github.com/pytorch/pytorch@f28ea6906201a754b307bc1d31b96d2ec05a912a/-/blob/test/higher_order_ops/test_print.py)\n\n"

If this\n240:         is true, we will create a token for every side effect type seen that\n241:         does not have a token assigned yet.  If this is false, the tokens\n242:         should've all been created ahead of time, so we will error if there is\n243:         no token mapping to every effect type.\n244: \n245:         tokens: Map of effect type to tokens. This is to chain operators of the\n246:         same effects together so that they do not get reordered in later\n247:         optimization passes.\n248:     \"\"\"\n249: \n250:     # Get a token. But the tokens should always exist during proxy mode tracing.\n253:     key = _get_effect(op)\n254:     if key is None:\n255:         raise AssertionError(f\"effect key must not be None for op {op}\")\n256:     if key not in tokens:\n257:         if not allow_token_discovery:\n258:             raise AssertionError(\n259:                 f\"Could not find a token for effect {key} which came from the function {op}\"\n260:             )\n261:         proxy_tensor_mode = torch._C._get_dispatch_mode(\n262:             torch._C._TorchDispatchModeKey.PROXY\n263:         )\n264:         if proxy_tensor_mode is not None:\n265:             # Format string with keyword arguments (named placeholders):\n       torch._higher_order_ops.print(\"moo {x} {y}\", x=1, y=2)\n       Output: \"moo 1 2\"\n\n    2. Format string with positional arguments (positional placeholders):\n       torch._higher_order_ops.print(\"moo {} {}\", 1, 2)\n       Output: \"moo 1 2\"\n\n    3. This is needed to ensure a traced graph from\n    AOTAutograd is functional so that future optimization passes do not reorder\n    these operators. This is done through threading \"effect tokens\" through the\n    graph to enforce data dependence between side effectful ops.\n\n    The tokens are basically dummy values (torch.tensor([])). We create a token\n    per \"effect type\", which are enumerated in the _EffectType enum.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(self) -> None:\n        super().__init__(\"with_effects\")\n\n    def __call__(\n        self,\n        token,\n        op: OpType,\n        *args: tuple[Any, ...],\n        **kwargs: dict[str, Any],\n    ) -> tuple[Any, ...]:\n        if not isinstance(op, (torch._ops.HigherOrderOperator, torch._ops.OpOverload)):\n            raise AssertionError(\n                f\"op must be HigherOrderOperator or OpOverload, got {type(op)}\"\n            )\n        if has_aliasing(op):\n            raise AssertionError(\"Ops with aliasing is not supported\")\n        if not isinstance(kwargs, dict):\n            raise AssertionError(f\"kwargs must be a dict, got {type(kwargs)}\")\n        # If this\n        is true, we will create a token for every side effect type seen that\n        does not have a token assigned yet.  If this is false, the tokens\n        should've all been created ahead of time, so we will error if there is\n        no token mapping to every effect type.\n\n        tokens: Map of effect type to tokens. This is to chain operators of the\n        same effects together so that they do not get reordered in later\n        optimization passes.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    # Get a token.         "+    def test_inductor_fusion_same_with_and_without_print(self):",
        "+        \"\"\"Test that Inductor fusion is the same with and without print HOP.",
        "+",
        "+        This validates that adding print HOPs doesn't change the fusion pattern -",

        "+        \"\"\"",
        "+        import re",
        "+",
        "+        # Function WITHOUT print",
        "+        def f_no_print(a, b, c):",
        "+            x = a * b",
        "+            y = x + c",
        "+            z = y**2",
        "+            return z",
        "+",
        "+        # Function WITH print (same computation, but with intermediate prints)",
        "+        def f_with_print(a, b, c):",
        "+            x = a * b",
        "+            torch._higher_order_ops.print(\"x: {}\", x)",
        "+            y = x + c",
        "+            z = y**2",
        "+            return z",
        "+",
        "+        a = torch.randn(4)",
        "+        b = torch.randn(4)",
        "+        c = torch.randn(4)",
        "+",
        "+        # Compile both versions",
        "+        compiled_no_print = torch.compile(f_no_print, backend=\"inductor\")",
        "+        compiled_with_print = torch.compile(f_with_print, backend=\"inductor\")",
        "+",
        "+        # Get generated code for both",
        "+        _, codes_no_print = run_and_get_code(compiled_no_print, a, b, c)",
        "+        with patch(\"sys.stdout\", new_callable=io.StringIO):",
        "+            _, codes_with_print = run_and_get_code(compiled_with_print, a, b, c)",
        "+",
        "+        merged_no_print = \"\\n\".join(codes_no_print)",
        "+        merged_with_print = \"\\n\".join(codes_with_print)",
        "+",
        "+        # Extract kernel names - pattern matches names like \"cpp_fused_add_mul_pow_0\"",
        "+        kernel_pattern = r\"cpp_fused_([\\w_]+?)_\\d+\"",
        "+",
        "+        # Extract the fusion patterns (the ops being fused, not including the trailing number)",
        "+        def extract_fusion_ops(code):",
        "+            \"\"\"Extract the set of fused operation patterns from kernel names.\"\"\"",
        "+            matches = re.findall(kernel_pattern, code)",
        "+            # Each match is the ops part like \"add_mul_pow\"",
        "+            return set(matches)",
        "+",
        "+        fusion_ops_no_print = extract_fusion_ops(merged_no_print)",
        "+        fusion_ops_with_print = extract_fusion_ops(merged_with_print)",
        "+",
        "+        # Verify that the fusion patterns are the same",
        "+        # The print version should have the same fused ops as the no-print version",

        "+            fusion_ops_no_print,",
        "+            fusion_ops_with_print,",

        "+",
        "+        # Verify the with_print version has print calls",
        "+        self.assertIn(\"print(\", merged_with_print)",

        "+        result_no_print = compiled_no_print(a, b, c)",
        "+        with patch(\"sys.stdout\", new_callable=io.StringIO):",
        "+            result_with_print = compiled_with_print(a, b, c)",
        "+        self.assertTrue(torch.allclose(result_no_print, result_with_print))",

class Print(HigherOrderOperator):
    """
    print(format_str, **kwargs) -> None

    This Higher Order Operator (HOP) provides a functional version of print for use in PyTorch graphs.
    It enables format printing with named arguments, e.g., torch._higher_order_ops.print("moo {x} {y}", x=1, y=2).

    This HOP enables printing without causing graph break.
    """

    def __init__(self) -> None:
        super().__init__("print")

    def __call__(self, format_str: str, **kwargs: object) -> None:
        assert isinstance(format_str, str)
        return super().__call__(format_str, **kwargs)
After
class Print(HigherOrderOperator):
    """
    print(format_str, *args, **kwargs) -> None

    This Higher Order Operator (HOP) provides a functional version of print for use in PyTorch graphs.
    It supports the calling conventions of print(format_str.format(*args, **kwargs)):

    1. Format string with keyword arguments (named placeholders):
       torch._higher_order_ops.print("moo {x} {y}", x=1, y=2)
       Output: "moo 1 2"

    2. Format string with positional arguments (positional placeholders):
       torch._higher_order_ops.print("moo {} {}", 1, 2)
       Output: "moo 1 2"

    3. Mixed positional and keyword arguments:
       torch._higher_order_ops.print("moo {} {y}", 1, y=2)
       Output: "moo 1 2"

    This HOP enables printing without causing graph break.
    """

    def __init__(self) -> None:
        super().__init__("print")

    def __call__(self, format_str: str, *args: object, **kwargs: object) -> None:
        if not isinstance(format_str, str):
            raise AssertionError(f"format_str must be a string, got {type(format_str)}")
        # pyrefly: ignore [missing-attribute]
        return super().__call__(format_str, *args, **kwargs)
2. EDIT /workspace/torch/_higher_order_ops/print.py

    # pyrefly: ignore [bad-override]
    def gen_schema(self, format_str: str, **kwargs: object) -> torch.FunctionSchema:
        from torch._higher_order_ops.schema import HopSchemaGenerator

        schema_gen = HopSchemaGenerator(self)
        schema_gen.add_arg("format_str", format_str[0])

        # Add each kwarg as a keyword-only argument
        for key, value in kwargs.items():
            schema_gen.add_arg(key, value, kw_only=True)

        schema_gen.add_schema_tree_spec(format_str, **kwargs)

        return schema_gen.gen_schema()
After
    # pyrefly: ignore [bad-override]
    def gen_schema(
        self, format_str: str, *args: object, **kwargs: object
    ) -> torch.FunctionSchema:
        from torch._higher_order_ops.schema import HopSchemaGenerator

        schema_gen = HopSchemaGenerator(self)
        schema_gen.add_arg("format_str", format_str[0])

        # Add each positional arg
        for i, value in enumerate(args):
            schema_gen.add_arg(f"arg{i}", value)

        # Add each kwarg as a keyword-only argument
        for key, value in kwargs.items():
            schema_gen.add_arg(key, value, kw_only=True)

        schema_gen.add_schema_tree_spec(format_str, *args, **kwargs)

        return schema_gen.gen_schema()

@print.py_impl(torch._C.DispatchKey.CompositeExplicitAutograd)
# pyre-ignore
def print_impl(format_str: str, **kwargs: object) -> None:
    # Ensure all immutable_dict/list in kwargs are converted to regular dict/list
    map_types: dict[type, type] = {
        torch.fx.immutable_collections.immutable_dict: dict,
        torch.fx.immutable_collections.immutable_list: list,
    }
    new_kwargs = pytree.tree_map_only(
        tuple(map_types.keys()),
        lambda a: map_types[type(a)](a),
        kwargs,
        lambda a: isinstance(a, tuple(map_types.keys())),
    )
    #  Use built-in print to avoid recursion with the HOP print
    builtins.print(format_str.format(**new_kwargs))
After
@print.py_impl(torch._C.DispatchKey.CompositeExplicitAutograd)
# pyre-ignore
def print_impl(format_str: str, *args: object, **kwargs: object) -> None:
    # Ensure all immutable_dict/list in args and kwargs are converted to regular dict/list
    map_types: dict[type, type] = {
        torch.fx.immutable_collections.immutable_dict: dict,
        torch.fx.immutable_collections.immutable_list: list,
    }
    new_args, new_kwargs = pytree.tree_map_only(
        tuple(map_types.keys()),
        lambda a: map_types[type(a)](a),
        (args, kwargs),
        lambda a: isinstance(a, tuple(map_types.keys())),
    )
    #  Use built-in print to avoid recursion with the HOP print
    builtins.print(format_str.format(*new_args, **new_kwargs))

    def __call__(
        self,
        token,
        op: OpType,
        *args: tuple[Any, ...],
        **kwargs: dict[str, Any],
    ) -> tuple[Any, ...]:
        if not isinstance(op, (torch._ops.HigherOrderOperator, torch._ops.OpOverload)):
            raise AssertionError(
                f"op must be HigherOrderOperator or OpOverload, got {type(op)}"
            )
        if has_aliasing(op):
            raise AssertionError("Ops with aliasing is not supported")
        if not isinstance(kwargs, dict):
            raise AssertionError(f"kwargs must be a dict, got {type(kwargs)}")
        # pyrefly: ignore [missing-attribute]
        return super().__call__(token, op, *args, **kwargs)

After
with_effects.fallthrough(DispatchKey.AutogradCPU)
with_effects.fallthrough(DispatchKey.AutogradCUDA)


@with_effects.py_functionalize_impl
def with_effects_functional(
    ctx,
    token: torch.Tensor,
    op: torch._ops.OpOverload,
    *args: tuple[Any, ...],
    **kwargs: dict[str, Any],
) -> tuple[torch.Tensor, ...]:
    # with_effects is already functional, so just re-emit it.
    unwrapped_token, unwrapped_args, unwrapped_kwargs = ctx.unwrap_tensors(
        [token, args, kwargs]
    )
    with ctx.redispatch_to_next():
        result = with_effects(unwrapped_token, op, *unwrapped_args, **unwrapped_kwargs)
    return ctx.wrap_tensors(result)

Before
    # Get a token. We can't do `tokens.get(op, torch.tensor([]))` because
    # this will create an empty tensor during proxy mode tracing if the token
    # doesn't exist. But the tokens should always exist during proxy mode tracing.
    key = _get_effect(op)

After
    # Get a token. We can't do `tokens.get(op, torch.tensor([]))` because
    # this will create an empty tensor during proxy mode tracing if the token
    # doesn't exist. But the tokens should always exist during proxy mode tracing.
    key = _get_effect(op)
    if key is None:
        raise AssertionError(f"effect key must not be None for op {op}")
    if key not in tokens:
        if not allow_token_discovery:
            raise AssertionError(
                f"Could not find a token for effect {key} which came from the function {op}"
            )

import io

import torch

@instantiate_parametrized_tests
class TestHopPrint(TestCase):
    def test_base_print(self):
        def f(x):
            x = x + x
            torch._higher_order_ops.print("moo")
            x = x * x
            torch._higher_order_ops.print("moo")
            return x

        x = torch.randn(3, 3)
        with patch("sys.stdout", new_callable=io.StringIO) as mock_stdout:
            f(x)
            printed_output = mock_stdout.getvalue().strip()

        self.assertEqual(printed_output, "moo\nmoo")

    def test_args_kwargs_print(self):
        """Test print with kwargs, positional args, and mixed args/kwargs."""

        # Test positional args, kwargs, and mixed only
        def f(x):
            x = x + x
            torch._higher_order_ops.print("moo kwargs {x} {y}", x=1, y=2)
            torch._higher_order_ops.print("moo args {} {}", 1, 2)
            torch._higher_order_ops.print("moo mixed {} {y}", 1, y=2)
            x = x * x
            return x

        x = torch.randn(3, 3)

        with patch("sys.stdout", new_callable=io.StringIO) as mock_stdout:
            f(x)
            printed_output = mock_stdout.getvalue().strip()
        self.assertEqual(printed_output, "moo kwargs 1 2\nmoo args 1 2\nmoo mixed 1 2")
